### <a id="Equation preservation">Equation preservation</a>

This is the [Base.Varieties.Preservation][] module of the [Agda Universal Algebra Library][]. In this module we show that identities are preserved by closure operators H, S, and P.  This will establish the easy direction of Birkhoff's HSP Theorem.

<pre class="Agda">

</pre>



#### <a id="closure-properties">Closure properties</a>

The types defined above represent operators with useful closure properties. We now prove a handful of such properties that we need later.

The next lemma would be too obvious to care about were it not for the fact that we'll need it later, so it too must be formalized.

<pre class="Agda">

#### <a id="PS-in-SP">PS(ùí¶) ‚äÜ SP(ùí¶)</a>

Finally, we are in a position to prove that a product of subalgebras of algebras in a class ùí¶ is a subalgebra of a product of algebras in ùí¶.

 <a id="6545" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#6545" class="Function">PS‚äÜSP</a> <a id="6551" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="6553" class="Comment">-- extensionality assumptions:</a>

  <a id="6620" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a>      <a id="6627" href="Base.Varieties.Closure.html#4634" class="Datatype">P</a><a id="6628" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="6629" #### <a id="more-class-inclusions">More class inclusions</a>

We conclude this subsection with three more inclusion relations that will have bit parts to play later (e.g., in the formal proof of Birkhoff's Theorem).

#### <a id="V-is-closed-under-lift">V is closed under lift</a>

As mentioned earlier, a technical hurdle that must be overcome when formalizing proofs in Agda is the proper handling of universe levels. In particular, in the proof of the Birkhoff's theorem, for example, we will need to know that if an algebra ùë® belongs to the variety V ùí¶, then so does the lift of ùë®.  Let us get the tedious proof of this technical lemma out of the way.

Above we proved that `SP(ùí¶) ‚äÜ V(ùí¶)`, and we did so under fairly general assumptions about the universe level parameters.  Unfortunately, this is sometimes not quite general enough, so we now prove the inclusion again for the specific universe parameters that align with subsequent applications of this result.


<pre class="Agda">

#### <a id="S-in-SP">‚®Ö S(ùí¶) ‚àà SP(ùí¶)</a>

Finally, we prove a result that plays an important role, e.g., in the formal proof of Birkhoff's Theorem. As we saw in [Base.Algebras.Products][], the (informal) product `‚®Ö S(ùí¶)` of all subalgebras of algebras in ùí¶ is implemented (formally) in the [agda-algebras](https://github.com/ualib/agda-algebras) library as `‚®Ö ùîÑ S(ùí¶)`. Our goal is to prove that this product belongs to `SP(ùí¶)`. We do so by first proving that the product belongs to `PS(ùí¶)` and then applying the `PS‚äÜSP` lemma.

Before doing so, we need to redefine the class product so that each factor comes with a map from the type `X` of variable symbols into that factor.  We will explain the reason for this below.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="10825" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="10826" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10826" class="Bound">fe‚ÇÇ</a> <a id="10830" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10832" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#954" class="Function">funext</a> <a id="10839" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10840" href="Base.Algebras.Products.html#3165" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="10843" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a><a id="10844" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="10846" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10847" href="Base.Algebras.Products.html#3165" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="10850" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a><a id="10851" class="Symbol">)}</a>

 <a id="10913" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10895" class="Function">‚Ñë&#39;</a> <a id="10916" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="10918" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">Œ£[</a> <a id="10921" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10921" class="Bound">ùë®</a> <a id="10923" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">‚àà</a> <a id="10925" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10926" href="Base.Algebras.Basic.html#6259" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="10934" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a> <a id="10936" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#633" class="Bound">ùëÜ</a><a id="10937" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="10939" href="Data.Product.html#916" class="Function">]</a> <a id="10941" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="10943" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10921" class="Bound">ùë®</a> <a id="10945" href="Relation.Unary.html#1523" class="Function Operator">‚àà</a> <a id="10947" href="Base.Varieties.Closure.html#4058" class="Datatype">S</a><a id="10948" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="10949" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a><a id="10950" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="10952" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a><a id="10953" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="10955" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10856" class="Bound">ùí¶</a><a id="10956" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="10958" href="Data.Product.html#1167" class="Function Operator">√ó</a> <a id="10960" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="10961" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10731" class="Bound">X</a> <a id="10963" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="10965" href="Base.Overture.Preliminaries.html#4402" class="Function Operator">‚à£</a> <a id="10967" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10921" class="Bound">ùë®</a> <a id="10969" href="Base.Overture.Preliminaries.html#4402" class="Function Operator">‚à£</a><a id="10970" class="Symbol">))</a>

</pre>

Notice that the second component of this dependent pair type is  `(ùë® ‚àà ùí¶) √ó (X ‚Üí ‚à£ ùë® ‚à£)`. In previous versions of the [UALib][] this second component was simply `ùë® ‚àà ùí¶`, until we realized that adding the type `X ‚Üí ‚à£ ùë® ‚à£` is quite useful. Later we will see exactly why, but for now suffice it to say that a map of type `X ‚Üí ‚à£ ùë® ‚à£` may be viewed abstractly as an *ambient context*, or more concretely, as an assignment of *values* in `‚à£ ùë® ‚à£` to *variable symbols* in `X`.  When computing with or reasoning about products, while we don't want to rigidly impose a context in advance, want do want to lay our hands on whatever context is ultimately assumed.  Including the "context map" inside the index type `‚Ñë` of the product turns out to be a convenient way to achieve this flexibility.


Taking the product over the index type `‚Ñë` requires a function that maps an index `i : ‚Ñë` to the corresponding algebra.  Each `i : ‚Ñë` is a triple, say, `(ùë® , p , h)`, where `ùë® : Algebra Œ± ùëÜ`, `p : ùë® ‚àà ùí¶`, and `h : X ‚Üí ‚à£ ùë® ‚à£`, so the function mapping an index to the corresponding algebra is simply the first projection.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="class-products-with-maps.ùîÑ&#39;"></a><a id="12109" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12109" class="Function">ùîÑ&#39;</a> <a id="12112" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12114" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10895" class="Function">‚Ñë&#39;</a> <a id="12117" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="12119" href="Base.Algebras.Basic.html#6259" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="12127" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a> <a id="12129" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#633" class="Bound">ùëÜ</a>
 <a id="12132" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12109" class="Function">ùîÑ&#39;</a> <a id="12135" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12137" class="Symbol">Œª</a> <a id="12139" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12140" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12140" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="12142" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12144" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10895" class="Function">‚Ñë&#39;</a><a id="12146" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="12148" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="12150" href="Base.Overture.Preliminaries.html#4402" class="Function Operator">‚à£</a> <a id="12152" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12140" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="12154" href="Base.Overture.Preliminaries.html#4402" class="Function Operator">‚à£</a>

</pre>

Finally, we define `class-product` which represents the product of all members of ùí¶.

<pre class="Agda">

 <a id="class-products-with-maps.class-product&#39;"></a><a id="12270" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12270" class="Function">class-product&#39;</a> <a id="12285" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12287" href="Base.Algebras.Basic.html#6259" class="Function">Algebra</a> <a id="12295" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12296" href="Base.Algebras.Products.html#3165" class="Function">ov</a> <a id="12299" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#10718" class="Bound">Œ±</a><a id="12300" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="12302" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#633" class="Bound">ùëÜ</a>
 <a id="12305" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12270" class="Function">class-product&#39;</a> <a id="12320" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12322" href="Base.Algebras.Products.html#1899" class="Function">‚®Ö</a> <a id="12324" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#12109" class="Function">ùîÑ&#39;</a>

</pre>

If `p : ùë® ‚àà ùí¶` and `h : X ‚Üí ‚à£ ùë® ‚à£`, we view the triple `(ùë® , p , h) ‚àà ‚Ñë` as an index over the class, and so we can think of `ùîÑ (ùë® , p , h)` (which is simply `ùë®`) as the projection of the product `‚®Ö ùîÑ` onto the `(ùë® , p, h)`-th component.

So, since `PS‚äÜSP`, we see that that the product of all subalgebras of a class `ùí¶` belongs to `SP(ùí¶)`.

<pre class="Agda">

</pre>


#### <a id="h-preserves-identities">H preserves identities</a>

First we prove that the closure operator H is compatible with identities that hold in the given class.

<pre class="Agda">

<a id="13543" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="13548" href="Relation.Binary.PropositionalEquality.Core.html#2708" class="Module">‚â°-Reasoning</a>

<a id="13561" class="Keyword">private</a> <a id="13569" class="Keyword">variable</a> <a id="13578" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#13578" class="Generalizable">ùìß</a> <a id="13580" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13582" href="Agda.Primitive.html#597" class="Postulate">Level</a>

      <a id="14394" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14395" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#13812" class="Bound">ùë©</a> <a id="14397" href="Base.Terms.Operations.html#2637" class="Function Operator">‚ü¶</a> <a id="14399" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#13791" class="Bound">q</a> <a id="14401" href="Base.Terms.Operations.html#2637" class="Function Operator">‚üß</a><a id="14402" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14404" href="Base.Varieties.Preservation.html#13834" class="Bound">b</a>          <a id="14415" href="Relation.Binary.PropositionalEquality.Core.html#3105" class="Function Operator">‚àé</a>

</pre>

The converse of the foregoing result is almost too obvious to bother with. Nonetheless, we formalize it for completeness.

Again, the obvious converse is barely worth the bits needed to formalize it.

#### <a id="v-preserves-identities">V preserves identities</a>

Finally, we prove the analogous preservation lemmas for the closure operator `V`.

#### <a id="class-identities">Class identities</a>

From `V-id1` it follows that if ùí¶ is a class of structures, then the set of identities modeled by all structures in `ùí¶` is equivalent to the set of identities modeled by all structures in `V ùí¶`.  In other terms, `Th (V ùí¶)` is precisely the set of identities modeled by `ùí¶`.   We formalize this observation as follows.

<pre class="Agda">

Once again, and for the last time, completeness dictates that we formalize the coverse of `V-id1`, however obvious it may be.

<pre class="Agda">
